And yes, the book is about 900 pages long, but with each page being absolutely wonderful story-telling, one gets lost in the pages, and actually leaves one wanting, even crying for more.  But most of all, \\"11-22-63\\" title aside, this is a wonderful, tender, heart-felt, love story, and it is by far my favorite S. King novel.  I may even read it again, as I enjoyed the process so very much.  Read it for the sci-fi time travel story-line, or read it for the Oswald-Kennedy assassination line, or read it just to excape the present and experience a more innocent, kinder America of 1958-1963, but if you do not have tears in your eyes as you read the last page, you missed the point of the book.  And I am not a man who easily tears up.<br /><br />I loved this book, and once I got hooked (about page 5) I read it in two days.  I literally could not put it down until I reached the last page.  I think you will experience the same.<br /><br />Don't buy this book if you are looking for a treatise on the Kennedy assassination.  It is not that at all.  Buy it to experience the special, tender love shared between a man and a woman. This is the heart and soul of the book.<br /><br />kone

0385534639|4.0|I was immediately drawn into this book and couldn't put it down.  I really liked the structure and the variety of characters.  I was engaged by all their stories and never resented shifts between narrative perspective.  I also found the time changes were well used to build suspense and made the later interaction of characters brought together from different strands of the narrative much richer.  The circus itself was even better than I could have imagined.  So complex, so very interesting and beautiful.  I did find the overall story arc about the unspecified competition between the illusionists lacked a convincing motivation and I was surprised that these characters didn't rebel more, even though they were bound to their situation.  I liked the style of this book, which reminded me a bit of Angela Carter, but perhaps more direct.  I did find the occasional grammatical errors unfortunate and unnecessary - such a gifted writer should have a proper editor.  Whilst there is a dark undercurrent to this book, I actually found most of the characters surprisingly benign and cooperative, which balanced the mood well.  This book is crying out for an imaginative screen adaptation, although imagining its world was perhaps even more satisfying than seeing it would be.  I was sorry to finish this book!

B005HV6Y5W|5.0|If you want a quick guide on the artistic sensibility of someone, ask their opinion of The Tree of Life. Those who hate this film -- and they are virulent in their hatred -- are generally incapable of appreciating something unusual. They demand a simple plot, dialogue, A STORY!  Pay attention and you'll notice a very deep and profound story in this film, one about loss and how even the most carefully chosen beliefs and philosophies fail to prepare people for tragedy.   These scenes where \\"nothing happens\\" are some of the most astoundingly beautiful frames of film ever captured. So much story is condensed into these moments that you can understand the personality of the characters without the creation of cliched drama.  Proust once wrote that art creates its own audience. In a way, I'm glad that this movie has created so many angry detractors -- it's proof that Malick is up to something big and important. It reminds me of how 2001: A Space Odyssey and Raging Bull were treated by average viewers when they first played in theaters.  Fifteen years from now, The Tree of Life will be the only film of 2011 that anyone remembers. And those who so public, angrily denounced it will slowly delete their screeds against it in silence.

The one common thread throughout history and the book is that Steve Jobs played a forward and largely dominant role in the devices and technology we all enjoy today.  When he died, I thought \\"Wow!, the innovation will die with him...\\"  I'm encouraged through Isaacson's accounting that such will not be the case.  As he surrounded himself with outstanding creative minds, these people could continue on without his leadership... This book affirmed my reasoning for not purchasing Apple products and opened my mind as to why I might consider a change in the future.  After reading this book and getting a better understanding of Apple products from the people who created them (not just Steve Jobs' perspective), I can see where the benefits lie and if my family had started out as an \\"Apple\\" family, we would be set with all the products to integrate all of the ease and wonder put into them...  Will I buy \\"Apple\\" products in the future?  Hard to say.  Did this book convince me that they are worth it?  I'm waffling.  What this book did do is take me on a trip down memory lane of how Apple technology moved through the 80's, 90's and 2000's -- a trip worth revisiting.  The most exciting take from the book is the move toward a more \\"digital\\" education where kids aren't packing around 100 pounds in text books...  the future of learning... and the comment from Steve Jobs to \\"keep moving\\" and from Bob Dylan \\"if you're not busy being born, you're busy dying.\\"    I recommend this book to anyone curious about Steve Jobs and everyone who wants to read a bit of history on the growth of technology (Apple, Pixar, Disney, etc.)  It left me wanting to read a similar book (if someone will write it) about Microsoft and the \\"real\\" Bill Gates..., Intel, Oracle, and other founders of lasting technology giants of industry that drive our personal and professional worlds.

The students are bound together for the duration of the challenge, unable to walk away or escape. The venue chosen for this particular challenge is a circus. The two contestants, Marco and Celia (both bound to the contest as young children), eventually meet and fall in love. Cricket might have a chance if he was only making up for his mistakes, but he also has to make amends for what damage his sister caused all those years ago.<br /><br />Cricket meets a little known character, St. Clair, at Berkley. They become quick friends...as everyone does with St. Clair. This works to Cricket's advantage since Anna is Lola's manager at the movie theater. I love that Stephanie included St. Clair and Anna in Lola and the Boy Next Door. They made a perfect avenue for Cricket to get closer to Lola. And who can resist St. Clair.<br /><br />Honestly, Cricket is one of my favorite characters ever. He is full of energy and shines like the sun. You just can't help but love him. Again, he is one of Stephanie's perfectly flawed characters. Cricket is weird in his own right, the crazy inventor type. Wild hair, a flair for the flamboyant, and good at everything he does - even though he can't see it. He's a bit insecure about himself...both because of past mistakes and a questionable heritage. He puts himself out there in ways that will cause him pain but he knows what he wants and if he is patient, perhaps he will get it.<br /><br />Stephanie Perkins is a master at creating beautifully weaved love stories. Love stories that make your heart ache with desire. You cannot not pull for these characters. Nothing about them is perfect and nothing comes easy. That's life, right? But Stephanie's stories flow at a perfect pace, never giving you that break you need to put the book down. I read bot Anna and the French Kiss and Lola and the Boy Next Door in one sitting. Well, one sitting each. Each time I thought about putting one down...I felt my heart break, needing to know how things would end. Because Stephanie makes her characters work for their happy endings, the chemistry and tension are always palpable on the pages.<br /><br />It wasn't until these books were recommended to me by some fellow bloggers that I started reading an YA Contemporary...now I seek these books out.<br /><br />One last thing, I want to say thank you to Stephanie for including a bit about alternative lifestyles in this book. I have family who belong to the LGBT community and it is important to me that their lives are acknowledged in a positive and loving way. I liked how quick of a read it was even though it's really long. I also got invested in the characters and what would happen to them, which means a lot in a book where a lot of them have to die!  The first person narrative was fun because it'd been a while since I read something that wasn't third person, and it got me to relate more with Katniss. It was difficult rooting for both her and the other characters in The Games.<br /><br />The only thing I wish could have been featured more were more details on the other characters in The Games. I felt that sometimes they were killed off too quickly just to get them out of the way and focus more on the central characters in the competition. I'd have liked if there were more fights and kills that were explained, described or shown. I also felt like the ending was a little bit too much of a cliffhanger, but I guess that just makes me more motivated to pick up the second one in the series.<br /><br />Overall, I'd recommend this book to my friends looking for a fun, easy read. It's not terribly difficult to get through and the story and characters keep you interested to keep going. The writing is also nice because it's not as elementary as \\"Twilight\\" but equal/a little more elevated than \\"Harry Potter.\\" For me, the most interesting part of this book was the romance arch with Katniss, Peeta and Gale.
